                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlXEg2g6x73w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kundu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Talie, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duffort, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L. F.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">54</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">3431</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">3448</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.201410376</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DKundu%252C%2BD.%253B%2BTalie%252C%2BE.%253B%2BDuffort%252C%2BV.%253B%2BNazar%252C%2BL.%2BF.Angew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%2B2015%252C%2B54%252C%2B3431%25E2%2580%25933448&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.201410376&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201200691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Slater, M. D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lee, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Johnson, C. T.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">9550</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">9555</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA00828J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DWang%252C%2BN.%253B%2BMa%252C%2BX.%253B%2BWang%252C%2BY.%253B%2BYang%252C%2BJ.%253B%2BQian%252C%2BY.%2BT.J.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%2B2015%252C%2B3%252C%2B9550%25E2%2580%25939555&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA00828J&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous MnFe2O4 microrods as advanced anodes for Li-ion batteries with long cycle lifespan</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Ma, Xiaojian; Wang, Yunpo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9550-9555</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous electrode materials with both high rate capabilities and long cycle lives are significant to satisfy the urgent demand of energy storage.  Furthermore, a one dimensional structure can facilitate Li+ diffusion and accommodate the vol. expansion.  Here, porous MnFe2O4 microrods have been successfully synthesized by a room temp. reaction and then moderate annealing in an Ar atm.  The porous MnFe2O4 electrodes exhibit high reversible capacity and outstanding cycling stability (after 1000 cycles still maintain about 630 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 1 A g-1), as well as high coulombic efficiency (&gt;98%).  Moreover, even at a high c.d. of 4 A g-1, the porous MnFe2O4 microrods can still maintain a reversible capacity of 420 mA h g-1.  These results demonstrate that the porous MnFe2O4 microrods are promising anode materials for high performance Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWb9zmIJ9-6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj5K5b3Mj9bzA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXks1aqt7o%253D&amp;md5=f828ce0bb5cd0b7b3608c4a2eb88b8a9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/c3cp50220a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zai, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, X.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Spinel One-Dimensional Architectures by Single-Spinneret Electrospinning for Energy Storage Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Shengjie; Li, Linlin; Hu, Yuxiang; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun; Ramakrishna, Seeram</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1945-1954</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and general method is developed to fabricate one-dimensional (1D) spinel composite oxides with complex architectures by using a facile single-spinneret electrospinning technique.  It is found that precursor polymers and heating rates could control the structures of the products, such as 1D solid, nanotube and tube-in-tubes structures.  Esp., the tube-in-tube structures have been successfully fabricated for various mixed metal oxide, including CoMn2O4, NiCo2O4, CoFe2O4, NiMn2O4 and ZnMn2O4.  Benefiting from the unique structure features, the tube-in-tube hollow nanostructures possess superior electrochem. performances in asym. supercapacitors and Li-O2 batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRNWPfV-xaNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixRtyQTcEumQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFylsrs%253D&amp;md5=1c0ab61bad4e45e18527c14b6f5aa701</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">14209</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">14221</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li- and Na-reduction products of meso-Co3O4 form high-rate, stably cycling battery anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klavetter, Kyle. C.; Garcia, Stephany; Dahal, Naween; Snider, Jonathan L.; Pedro de Souza, J.; Cell, Trevor H.; Cassara, Mark A.; Heller, Adam; Humphrey, Simon M.; Mullins, C. Buddie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14209-14221</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High surface area (367 m2 g-1) meso-porous Co3O4 was studied as the precursor of the anode material for Li and also Na ion batteries.  Co3O4 is considered a potential anode material due to its theor. capacity of 890 mA h g-1, over twice that of graphite.  This comparatively higher capacity can be safely charged at rapid rates owing to a relatively high Li-insertion potentials, but, consequently, the discharged energy is yielded at an av. potential near 2 V vs.  Li/Li+, with full Li-extn. achieved over a continuum of potentials up to 3 V.  The products of the Li redn. of Co3O4 cycle stably from 0.01 - 3.0 V vs.  Li/Li+ with 600 - 900 mA h g-1 capacity retention at C rates from 1-5; the products of its Na redn. cycle stably from 0.01-3.0 V vs.  Na/Na+ at C-rates up to 1 C with a lower 150 - 400 mA h g-1 capacity retention owing to greater ionic impedance.  TEM, SAED and XRD were used to examine the cycled material and the stable performance is attributed to finding that the mesoporous structure is retained.  Evaluation of five electrolyte formulations testing EC, FEC and Cl-EC showed that the stable meso-porous structure was best cycled with 5% FEC in EC:DEC at high charge/discharge rates, retaining 77% of its initial capacity at 5 C in a rate test.  Comparison of the a.c. impedance spectra and of the XPS of the SEIs formed in the presence and in the absence of 5 vol.% FEC shows that the SEI formed in the presence of FEC contains LiF and its carbonate layer is thinner than that formed in its absence, resulting in lesser impedance to Li migration through the SEI and facile ion de-solvation, improving the cycling performance.  In cycling stability tests with EC:DEC, irregular cycling behavior attributable to abrupt rises in cell resistance was regularly obsd. after testing over a few hundred cycles.  Long-term cycling irregularities are inhibited by halogenated solvents and completely eliminated by adding fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1Bhct3xriLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lixRtyQTcEumQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFCiur3I&amp;md5=42b0a0e8878afe7a0533af0f72136084</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR06432A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2770</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2776</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11004</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11015</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Nanosheet Frameworks Derived from Peat Moss as High Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Jia; Wang, Huanlei; Li, Zhi; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Cui, Kai; Xu, Zhanwei; Zahiri, Beniamin; Tan, Xuehai; Lotfabad, Elmira Memarzadeh; Olsen, Brian C.; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11004-11015</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Peat moss, a wild plant that covers 3% of the earth's surface, serves as an ideal precursor to create Na ion battery (NIB) anodes with some of the most attractive electrochem. properties ever reported for carbonaceous materials.  By inheriting the unique cellular structure of peat moss leaves, the resultant materials are composed of 3-dimensional macroporous interconnected networks of C nanosheets (as thin as 60 nm).  The peat moss tissue is highly cross-linked, being rich in lignin and hemicellulose, suppressing the nucleation of equil. graphite even at 1100°.  Rather, the carbons form highly ordered pseudographitic arrays with substantially larger intergraphene spacing (0.388 nm) than graphite (c/2 = 0.3354 nm).  XRD anal. demonstrates that this allows for significant Na intercalation to occur even &lt;0.2 V vs. Na/Na+.  By also incorporating a mild (300°) air activation step, the authors introduce hierarchical micro- and mesoporosity that tremendously improves the high rate performance through facile electrolyte access and further reduced Na ion diffusion distances.  The optimized structures (carbonization at 1100° + activation) result in a stable cycling capacity of 298 mA-h g-1 (after 10 cycles, 50 mA g-1), with ∼150 mA-h g-1 of charge accumulating between 0.1 and 0.001 V with negligible voltage hysteresis in that region, nearly 100% cycling Coulombic efficiency, and superb cycling retention and high rate capacity (255 mA-h g-1 at the 210th cycle, stable capacity of 203 mA-h g-1 at 500 mA g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9g5dheVSGj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcaGupIavnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslaqu7fJ&amp;md5=b76be05b1aa18433cf841293ee9cafb0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2978"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jeon, K. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Moon, H. R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ruminski, A. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kisielowski, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bardhan, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Urban, J.                 10.1038/nmat2978</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DJeon%252C%2BK.%2BJ.%253B%2BMoon%252C%2BH.%2BR.%253B%2BRuminski%252C%2BA.%2BM.%253B%2BJiang%252C%2BB.%253B%2BKisielowski%252C%2BC.%253B%2BBardhan%252C%2BR.%253B%2BUrban%252C%2BJ.%2BJ.Nat.%2BMater.%2B2011%252C%2B10%252C%2B286%25E2%2580%2593290&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fnmat2978&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                10.1038/srep04229</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar%3Fhl%3Den%26q%3DLiu%252C%2BB.%253B%2BHu%252C%2BX.%253B%2BXu%252C%2BH.%253B%2BLuo%252C%2BW.%253B%2BSun%252C%2BY.%253B%2BHuang%252C%2BY.%2BH.Sci.%2BRep.%2B2014%252C%2B4%252C%2B4229&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.6b00942&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fsrep04229&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulation of MnO nanocrystals in electrospun carbon nanofibers as high-performance anode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu Bin; Hu Xianluo; Xu Henghui; Luo Wei; Sun Yongming; Huang Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4229</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel and controllable approach is developed for the synthesis of MnO nanocrystals embedded in carbon nanofibers (MnO/CNFs) through an electrospinning process.  The as-formed MnO/CNFs have a porous structure with diameters of 100-200 nm and lengths up to several millimeters.  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, the resulting MnO/CNFs exhibit superior electrochemical performances with high specific capacity, good cyclability, and excellent rate capability.  The unique porous carbon nanofibers (PCNFs) can not only improve the contact area between the electrode and the electrolyte, but also alleviate the impact of the large volume effect of MnO during the electrochemical cycling.  It is expected that the present synthetic strategy can be extended to synthesize other nanostructured oxides encapsulated in carbon nanofibers for extensive energy transfer and storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSiD0byK_MmNMuCWE5mhx1RfW6udTcc2eYsbEkwGggeC7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2crgs1Sgsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=8e6851a9a54516f4ea00800af6cf0fda</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1021/nn200493r"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Murali, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stoller, M. H.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4350</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4358</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Catalyst-Free Synthesis of Nitrogen-Doped Graphene via Thermal Annealing Graphite Oxide with Melamine and Its Excellent Electrocatalysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sheng, Zhen-Huan; Shao, Lin; Chen, Jing-Jing; Bao, Wen-Jing; Wang, Feng-Bin; Xia, Xing-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4350-4358</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electronic and chem. properties of graphene can be modulated by chem. doping foreign atoms and functional moieties.  The general approach to the synthesis of N-doped graphene (NG), such as CVD performed in gas phases, requires transitional metal catalysts which could contaminate the resultant products and thus affect their properties.  The authors propose a facile, catalyst-free thermal annealing approach for large-scale synthesis of NG using low-cost industrial material melamine as the N source.  This approach can completely avoid the contamination of transition metal catalysts, and thus the intrinsic catalytic performance of pure NGs can be studied.  Detailed x-ray photoelectron spectrum anal. of the resultant products shows that the at. percentage of N in doped graphene samples can be adjusted up to 10.1%.  Such a high doping level was not reported previously.  High-resoln. N1s spectra reveal that the as-made NG mainly contains pyridine-like N atoms.  Electrochem. characterizations clearly demonstrate excellent electrocatalytic activity of NG toward the O redn. reaction (ORR) in alk. electrolytes, which is independent of N doping level.  The present catalyst-free approach opens up the possibility for the synthesis of NG in gram-scale for electronic devices and cathodic materials for fuel cells and biosensors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKDRCYrgQv07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljZcaGupIavnQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXmt1Gmu7w%253D&amp;md5=8f26d36950027b36706f9c9a35148c81</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR01281C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Z. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pasta, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yuan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                 10.1038/nnano.2015.194</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A phosphorene-graphene hybrid material as a high-capacity anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Jie; Lee, Hyun-Wook; Pasta, Mauro; Yuan, Hongtao; Zheng, Guangyuan; Sun, Yongming; Li, Yuzhang; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">980-985</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries have recently attracted significant attention as an alternative to Li-ion batteries because Na sources do not present the geopolitical issues that Li sources might.  Although recent reports on cathode materials for Na-ion batteries demonstrated performances comparable to their Li-ion counterparts, the major scientific challenge for a competitive Na-ion battery technol. is to develop viable anode materials.  A hybrid material made out of a few phosphorene layers sandwiched between graphene layers shows a specific capacity of 2 440 mA h g-1 (calcd. using the mass of P only) at a c.d. of 0.05 A g-1 and an 83% capacity retention after 100 cycles while operating between 0 and 1.5 V.  Using in situ TEM and ex situ x-ray diffraction techniques, the authors explain the large capacity of the anode through a dual mechanism of intercalation of Na ions along the x axis of the phosphorene layers followed by the formation of a Na3P alloy.  The presence of graphene layers in the hybrid material works as a mech. backbone and an elec. highway, ensuring that a suitable elastic buffer space accommodates the anisotropic expansion of phosphorene layers along the y and z axial directions for stable cycling operation.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp8p8kp9p5tl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljGsauyXd4ocA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2ltrrM&amp;md5=23b94375b97b50394801c280ff017cb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kundu, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Talie, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Duffort, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nazar, L. T.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">9550</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">9555</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C5TA00828J</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous MnFe2O4 microrods as advanced anodes for Li-ion batteries with long cycle lifespan</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Nana; Ma, Xiaojian; Wang, Yunpo; Yang, Jian; Qian, Yitai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9550-9555</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous electrode materials with both high rate capabilities and long cycle lives are significant to satisfy the urgent demand of energy storage.  Furthermore, a one dimensional structure can facilitate Li+ diffusion and accommodate the vol. expansion.  Here, porous MnFe2O4 microrods have been successfully synthesized by a room temp. reaction and then moderate annealing in an Ar atm.  The porous MnFe2O4 electrodes exhibit high reversible capacity and outstanding cycling stability (after 1000 cycles still maintain about 630 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 1 A g-1), as well as high coulombic efficiency (&gt;98%).  Moreover, even at a high c.d. of 4 A g-1, the porous MnFe2O4 microrods can still maintain a reversible capacity of 420 mA h g-1.  These results demonstrate that the porous MnFe2O4 microrods are promising anode materials for high performance Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWb9zmIJ9-6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8WlDtA4UbHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXks1aqt7o%253D&amp;md5=f828ce0bb5cd0b7b3608c4a2eb88b8a9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1039/c3cp50220a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zai, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Han, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, X.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.                         rightTab-cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fabrication of Spinel One-Dimensional Architectures by Single-Spinneret Electrospinning for Energy Storage Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Shengjie; Li, Linlin; Hu, Yuxiang; Srinivasan, Madhavi; Cheng, Fangyi; Chen, Jun; Ramakrishna, Seeram</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1945-1954</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile and general method is developed to fabricate one-dimensional (1D) spinel composite oxides with complex architectures by using a facile single-spinneret electrospinning technique.  It is found that precursor polymers and heating rates could control the structures of the products, such as 1D solid, nanotube and tube-in-tubes structures.  Esp., the tube-in-tube structures have been successfully fabricated for various mixed metal oxide, including CoMn2O4, NiCo2O4, CoFe2O4, NiMn2O4 and ZnMn2O4.  Benefiting from the unique structure features, the tube-in-tube hollow nanostructures possess superior electrochem. performances in asym. supercapacitors and Li-O2 batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqRNWPfV-xaNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8WlDtA4UbHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFylsrs%253D&amp;md5=1c0ab61bad4e45e18527c14b6f5aa701</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201503015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y. C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Garcia, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dahal, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Snider, J. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mullins, C. B.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Mater. Chem. A</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">2</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">14209</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">14221</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4TA02684E</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li- and Na-reduction products of meso-Co3O4 form high-rate, stably cycling battery anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klavetter, Kyle. C.; Garcia, Stephany; Dahal, Naween; Snider, Jonathan L.; Pedro de Souza, J.; Cell, Trevor H.; Cassara, Mark A.; Heller, Adam; Humphrey, Simon M.; Mullins, C. Buddie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14209-14221</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High surface area (367 m2 g-1) meso-porous Co3O4 was studied as the precursor of the anode material for Li and also Na ion batteries.  Co3O4 is considered a potential anode material due to its theor. capacity of 890 mA h g-1, over twice that of graphite.  This comparatively higher capacity can be safely charged at rapid rates owing to a relatively high Li-insertion potentials, but, consequently, the discharged energy is yielded at an av. potential near 2 V vs.  Li/Li+, with full Li-extn. achieved over a continuum of potentials up to 3 V.  The products of the Li redn. of Co3O4 cycle stably from 0.01 - 3.0 V vs.  Li/Li+ with 600 - 900 mA h g-1 capacity retention at C rates from 1-5; the products of its Na redn. cycle stably from 0.01-3.0 V vs.  Na/Na+ at C-rates up to 1 C with a lower 150 - 400 mA h g-1 capacity retention owing to greater ionic impedance.  TEM, SAED and XRD were used to examine the cycled material and the stable performance is attributed to finding that the mesoporous structure is retained.  Evaluation of five electrolyte formulations testing EC, FEC and Cl-EC showed that the stable meso-porous structure was best cycled with 5% FEC in EC:DEC at high charge/discharge rates, retaining 77% of its initial capacity at 5 C in a rate test.  Comparison of the a.c. impedance spectra and of the XPS of the SEIs formed in the presence and in the absence of 5 vol.% FEC shows that the SEI formed in the presence of FEC contains LiF and its carbonate layer is thinner than that formed in its absence, resulting in lesser impedance to Li migration through the SEI and facile ion de-solvation, improving the cycling performance.  In cycling stability tests with EC:DEC, irregular cycling behavior attributable to abrupt rises in cell resistance was regularly obsd. after testing over a few hundred cycles.  Long-term cycling irregularities are inhibited by halogenated solvents and completely eliminated by adding fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1Bhct3xriLbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8WlDtA4UbHA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtFCiur3I&amp;md5=42b0a0e8878afe7a0533af0f72136084</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1039/C4NR06432A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, N.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nanoscale</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2770</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2776</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C4NR06432A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mitlin, D.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">7</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">11004</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">11015</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn404640c</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Nanosheet Frameworks Derived from Peat Moss as High Performance Sodium Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Jia; Wang, Huanlei; Li, Zhi; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Cui, Kai; Xu, Zhanwei; Zahiri, Beniamin; Tan, Xuehai; Lotfabad, Elmira Memarzadeh; Olsen, Brian C.; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11004-11015</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Peat moss, a wild plant that covers 3% of the earth's surface, serves as an ideal precursor to create Na ion battery (NIB) anodes with some of the most attractive electrochem. properties ever reported for carbonaceous materials.  By inheriting the unique cellular structure of peat moss leaves, the resultant materials are composed of 3-dimensional macroporous interconnected networks of C nanosheets (as thin as 60 nm).  The peat moss tissue is highly cross-linked, being rich in lignin and hemicellulose, suppressing the nucleation of equil. graphite even at 1100°.  Rather, the carbons form highly ordered pseudographitic arrays with substantially larger intergraphene spacing (0.388 nm) than graphite (c/2 = 0.3354 nm).  XRD anal. demonstrates that this allows for significant Na intercalation to occur even &lt;0.2 V vs. Na/Na+.  By also incorporating a mild (300°) air activation step, the authors introduce hierarchical micro- and mesoporosity that tremendously improves the high rate performance through facile electrolyte access and further reduced Na ion diffusion distances.  The optimized structures (carbonization at 1100° + activation) result in a stable cycling capacity of 298 mA-h g-1 (after 10 cycles, 50 mA g-1), with ∼150 mA-h g-1 of charge accumulating between 0.1 and 0.001 V with negligible voltage hysteresis in that region, nearly 100% cycling Coulombic efficiency, and superb cycling retention and high rate capacity (255 mA-h g-1 at the 210th cycle, stable capacity of 203 mA-h g-1 at 500 mA g-1).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq9g5dheVSGj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYZDyZpJW1Bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslaqu7fJ&amp;md5=b76be05b1aa18433cf841293ee9cafb0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1038/nmat2978"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jeon, K. M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kisielowski, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bardhan, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Urban, J. H.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Sci. Rep.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">4</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4229</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/srep04229</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulation of MnO nanocrystals in electrospun carbon nanofibers as high-performance anode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu Bin; Hu Xianluo; Xu Henghui; Luo Wei; Sun Yongming; Huang Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4229</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel and controllable approach is developed for the synthesis of MnO nanocrystals embedded in carbon nanofibers (MnO/CNFs) through an electrospinning process.  The as-formed MnO/CNFs have a porous structure with diameters of 100-200 nm and lengths up to several millimeters.  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, the resulting MnO/CNFs exhibit superior electrochemical performances with high specific capacity, good cyclability, and excellent rate capability.  The unique porous carbon nanofibers (PCNFs) can not only improve the contact area between the electrode and the electrolyte, but also alleviate the impact of the large volume effect of MnO during the electrochemical cycling.  It is expected that the present synthetic strategy can be extended to synthesize other nanostructured oxides encapsulated in carbon nanofibers for extensive energy transfer and storage applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcSiD0byK_MmNMuCWE5mhx1RfW6udTcc2eZnO2KS2g1FNbntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2crgs1Sgsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=8e6851a9a54516f4ea00800af6cf0fda</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1021/nn200493r"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Murali, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stoller, M. H.</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ACS Nano</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">4350</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">4358</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn103584t</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Catalyst-Free Synthesis of Nitrogen-Doped Graphene via Thermal Annealing Graphite Oxide with Melamine and Its Excellent Electrocatalysis</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sheng, Zhen-Huan; Shao, Lin; Chen, Jing-Jing; Bao, Wen-Jing; Wang, Feng-Bin; Xia, Xing-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4350-4358</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electronic and chem. properties of graphene can be modulated by chem. doping foreign atoms and functional moieties.  The general approach to the synthesis of N-doped graphene (NG), such as CVD performed in gas phases, requires transitional metal catalysts which could contaminate the resultant products and thus affect their properties.  The authors propose a facile, catalyst-free thermal annealing approach for large-scale synthesis of NG using low-cost industrial material melamine as the N source.  This approach can completely avoid the contamination of transition metal catalysts, and thus the intrinsic catalytic performance of pure NGs can be studied.  Detailed x-ray photoelectron spectrum anal. of the resultant products shows that the at. percentage of N in doped graphene samples can be adjusted up to 10.1%.  Such a high doping level was not reported previously.  High-resoln. N1s spectra reveal that the as-made NG mainly contains pyridine-like N atoms.  Electrochem. characterizations clearly demonstrate excellent electrocatalytic activity of NG toward the O redn. reaction (ORR) in alk. electrolytes, which is independent of N doping level.  The present catalyst-free approach opens up the possibility for the synthesis of NG in gram-scale for electronic devices and cathodic materials for fuel cells and biosensors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrKDRCYrgQv07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYZDyZpJW1Bw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXmt1Gmu7w%253D&amp;md5=8f26d36950027b36706f9c9a35148c81</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR01281C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Feng, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, Z.         <script nonce="90f6e2797e3a775c-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

// LIT-455776 workaround
// Moving the popup before the header content for tab accessibility
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', () => {
    const headerNode = $('.header_content');
    const popupNode = $('.pairing-affiliations-popup');

<script nonce="90f6e2797e3a775c-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e2797e3a775c-SJC">

	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {

|\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e2797e3a775c-SJC">
var currentJournal = "Nano Letters";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90f6e2797e3a775c-SJC">
$(document).ready(function(){
    var cookie = "";
    var uri = "/doi/full/10.1021/html_original_uri?id=123";
    console.log("ACSPubs2 start");
    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){
                    cookie=cookie.concat(i+' = '+field+" - ");
                });
                
            } else {
                    cookie=status;
            }

            cookie1 = cookie;
            cookie = cookie1 + "; path=/; domain=.acs.org";
            //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
            $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
            console.log("ACSPubs2 success");
    })
    .fail(function(xx, status, err){
        cookie="error: 127.0.0.1";
        //document.cookie = "ACSPubs2= "+ btoa(cookie) ;
        $.cookie("ACSPubs2", btoa(cookie), {path: '/'}); // Session cookie valid across the entire site.
        console.log("ACSPubs2 failed");
        //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
    });
});
